{"nick":"joepie91","message":"laroi: a \"stream\" is a Node.js abstraction on top of event emitters, to represent some kind of eventually-ending stream of \"things\"","date":"2017-02-08T10:00:10.324Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"this can be either bytes (a regular stream) or objects (an object stream)","date":"2017-02-08T10:00:19.355Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"there are Readable streams and Writable streams, which are more or less self-explanatory","date":"2017-02-08T10:00:44.110Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"laroi","message":"Yep","date":"2017-02-08T10:00:49.520Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"one provides data and the other takes in data","date":"2017-02-08T10:00:53.583Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"then there's Duplex streams, which is a combined object that can act as a Readable *and* a Writable stream","date":"2017-02-08T10:01:07.371Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"but the two interfaces are not necessarily connected","date":"2017-02-08T10:01:11.855Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"laroi","message":"never heard of that","date":"2017-02-08T10:01:16.870Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"then there's Transform streams, which is just a Duplex stream where the interfaces *are* connected - specifically, you define a 'transform function' that is called for every \"thing\" sent to the Writable inteface, and the result is then put out on the Readable interface","date":"2017-02-08T10:01:52.718Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"then there's Passthrough streams, which are Transform streams that don't actually transform anything, and just immediately re-emit the original data","date":"2017-02-08T10:02:13.010Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"laroi: now, the reason why any of this matters:","date":"2017-02-08T10:02:17.892Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"when you're working with 8 gigs of data, like is the case here, you don't want to have all those 8 gigs in RAM at the same time","date":"2017-02-08T10:02:31.237Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"rather, you want a way to tell your mongodb library \"give me the items one by one and I will do something with them\" (in your case, transforming them to CSV lines)","date":"2017-02-08T10:02:55.425Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"similarly, you want to send the response to the client byte-by-byte","date":"2017-02-08T10:03:07.141Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"in what I am proposing:","date":"2017-02-08T10:03:22.845Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"* the MongoDB library provides a Readable stream for your query","date":"2017-02-08T10:03:31.256Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"* you define a Transform stream yourself for turning the objects from that Readable stream into 'flat' objects, key/value pairs","date":"2017-02-08T10:03:47.632Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"* you use the pre-made `csv` Transform stream to turn those flat objects into lines of CSV","date":"2017-02-08T10:03:58.862Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"* you then wire that up to a Writable stream - either the HTTP response (since that's a Writable stream too!) or a file on the filesystem, or wherever","date":"2017-02-08T10:04:30.421Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"laroi","message":"Got it","date":"2017-02-08T10:04:51.436Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"each individual item that comes from MongoDB first goes through your transform stream to be flattened, is then sent through `csv` to be turned into a single line of CSV, and is then sent as a bunch of bytes to the client","date":"2017-02-08T10:05:02.143Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"and so on and so on for the entire dataset","date":"2017-02-08T10:05:08.010Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"laroi","message":"Okay","date":"2017-02-08T10:05:11.210Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"result: you never have the entire dataset in RAM, you're only ever working on one item at a time","date":"2017-02-08T10:05:17.625Z","type":"message"}
